The Original Ruling of Divorce: Prohibition and Permissibility
Explains the original ruling of divorce as prohibition lifted by Sharia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original ruling (asl) of divorce in the Hanafi school and explain the proof that changed it to permissibility.

Core Idea
Divorce is originally prohibited; Sharia made it permissible but the prohibition is not entirely gone.

This lesson explores the foundational Hanafi position that divorce is not an unqualified good. The default is prohibition, but Allah permitted it with conditions. We will trace the shift from hazr to ibaha using Quranic evidence and understand why permission does not mean complete lifting of the original ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
Read the first sentence: 'الأصل فيه الحظر'. State that the default (asl) for divorce is prohibition (hazr).
This is before considering Sharia's allowance.
2
Note the Sharia change
The text says that prohibition was abandoned by Sharia, so permission became the legislated ruling. Understand that permission does not erase the original prohibition completely.
This sets divorce apart from acts that are purely mubah from the start.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Locate the verse (Al-Baqarah 2:236) cited: 'ولا جناح عليكم إن طلقتم النساء...' and the author's claim that it proves permissibility even without need.
Hanafi usul: 'لا جناح' (no sin) indicates ibaha.
4
Consider the counterpoint
The text mentions that some might interpret the verse as for need, but the author rejects this as incorrect. Recognize that the permission is general.
This strengthens the argument for permissibility without need.
5
Distinguish from marriage's asl
The passage compares with marriage: both originally prohibited, but marriage's prohibition was fully lifted for procreation, while divorce's prohibition remains in some sense.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the ethical weight of divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق الأصل فيه الحظر وترك ذلك بالشرع فصار الحل هو المشروع فهو نظير قول صاحب كشف الأسرار : إن الأصل في النكاح الحظر وإنما أبيح للحاجة إلى التوالد والتناسل، فهل يفهم منه أنه محظور فالحق إباحته لغير حاجة طلباً للخلاص منها لقوله تعالى ولا جناح عليكم إن طلقتم النساء ما لم تمسوهن ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٦] وحمله على الحاجة ليس بصحيح. وفي غاية البيان: يستحب طلاقها إذا كانت سليطة مؤذية أو تاركة للصلاة لا تقيم حدود الله تعالى اهـ. وهو يفيد جواز معاشرة من لا تصلي ولا إثم عليه بل عليها ولذا قالوا في الفتاوى : له أن يضربها على ترك الصلاة ولم يقولوا عليه مع أن في ضربها على تركها روايتين ذكرهما قاضيخان، فقد علمت أنه مباح ومستحب وسيأتي أنه حرام بدعي. ويكون واجباً إذا فات الإمساك بالمعروف كما في امرأة المجبوب والعنين بعد الطلب ولذا قالوا : إذا فاته الإمساك بالمعروف ناب القاضي منابه فوجب التسريح بالإحسان وأما شرطه في الزوج فالعقل والبلوغ، وفي الزوجة أن تكون منكوحته أو في عدته التي تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق وهي المعتدة بعدة الطلاق لا المعتدة بعدة الوطء والخلوة وحاصل ما في فتح القدير أن المعتدة التي هي محل للطلاق هي كل معتدة عن طلاق أو بعد تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وبعد ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً فقط، فلا يقع الطلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في هاتين، ولا يقع وينسب فاعله إلى الحمق لما فيه من كفران النعمة والإيذاء المنهي عنه فليست جهة الحظر ساقطة بالكلية كما يوهمه كلام البحر، ولذا كان أبغض الحلال بخلاف قولهم الأصل في النكاح الخطر فإن هذا الأصل ساقط فإنه حرام في الأصل لما فيه من الانتفاع بجزء الآدمي المحترم والاطلاع على العورات، وارتفع هذا الأصل لحاجة التوالد والتناسل وبقاء العالم. أما الأصل في الطلاق فإنه باق لم يسقط بالكلية فبين الأصلين بون بعيد لما قلنا من بقاء الحظر إذا كان بلا سبب أصلاً، ولا يمكن أن يحمل طلاق النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه رضي الله عنهم على فعله بلا سبب أصلاً بأن يكون لغواً وعبثاً بل لا بد من سبب معتبر شرعاً من الأعذار المذكورة ونحوها، فهذا تحقيق المقام بما لا مزيد عليه فاغتنمه والله الموفق
Book of Divorce: The original ruling in it is prohibition, and that was abandoned by the Sharia, so permission became the legislated ruling. It is similar to the statement of the author of Kashf al-Asrar: 'The original ruling in marriage is prohibition, and it was only permitted for the need of procreation and reproduction.' So is it understood from this that it is prohibited? The correct view is that it is permitted even without need, seeking relief from it, due to His statement: 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women while you have not touched them' [Al-Baqarah 2:236]. And interpreting it as for need is not correct. In Ghayat al-Bayan: It is recommended to divorce her if she is abusive and harmful or one who abandons prayer and does not uphold the limits of Allah. It indicates the permissibility of living with a woman who does not pray, with no sin on him but on her. Therefore they said in the Fatwas: He has the right to beat her for abandoning prayer, and they did not say it is upon him, although there are two narrations about beating her for abandoning it, mentioned by Qadikhan. So you have learned that it is permissible and recommended, and it will come later that it is forbidden and innovatory. And it becomes obligatory if good retention is missed, as in the case of a woman of a eunuch or impotent man after her request. Therefore they said: If he misses good retention, the judge takes his place, so he must release her with kindness. As for its condition in the husband: sanity and puberty. And in the wife: that she be his wife or in her waiting period that is a valid place for divorce, which is the waiting period after divorce, not the waiting period after intercourse or seclusion. The gist of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that the woman in waiting period who is a place for divorce is every woman in waiting period after divorce, or after the judge's separation due to one spouse's refusal to accept Islam, or after apostasy of one of them absolutely. So divorce does not occur in a waiting period from annulment except in those two cases, and it does not occur and its doer is attributed to foolishness because of the ingratitude of blessings and the prohibited harm. So the aspect of prohibition is not entirely abrogated, as the language of al-Bahr might suggest. Therefore it is the most hateful of permissible things, contrary to their statement that the original in marriage is danger, for this original is abrogated – it is originally prohibited due to deriving benefit from a respected human part and seeing private parts, and this original was lifted for the need of procreation and survival of the world. As for the original in divorce, it remains, not entirely abrogated, so there is a great difference between the two originals due to what we said of the persistence of prohibition when done without any reason. And it is impossible to attribute the divorce of the Prophet and his companions to doing it without any reason, as something futile and vain; rather, there must be a legally valid reason from the mentioned excuses and the like. So this is the verification of the matter without further addition; seize it, and Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe discussing the original ruling (hukm asli) of divorce. The author begins by stating that the default ruling of divorce is prohibition (hazr), but this prohibition was abandoned by the Sharia such that permission became the legislated ruling. He compares it to marriage, where the original ruling is also prohibition but permissibility came for the need of procreation. Then he clarifies that divorce is permitted even without need, based on the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah which indicates no sin in divorce before consummation. He then discusses recommended divorce (mustahabb) from Ghayat al-Bayan: if the wife is abusive or abandons prayer, it is recommended to divorce her. This also implies that living with such a woman is permissible without sin on the husband. He mentions fatwas about beating her for abandoning prayer. Then he discusses obligatory divorce (wajib) when good retention is missed, like in cases of impotence, and the judge may compel divorce. Then he lists conditions for the husband (sanity, puberty) and wife (being in a valid marriage or in a waiting period from divorce). He notes that a waiting period from annulment (faskh) does not allow divorce except in two cases: separation due to refusal of Islam or apostasy. He emphasizes that the prohibition aspect of divorce is not entirely lifted, which is why it is called the most hateful of permissible things. In contrast, the original prohibition in marriage is completely lifted for the need of procreation. The author concludes that divorce must have a valid reason; it cannot be futile, as the Prophet and his companions only divorced for valid reasons. The passage is rich in legal reasoning and defines the boundaries of permissible divorce.

Key Terms
الأصل في الطلاق (al-asl fi al-talaq): The default legal ruling of divorce before Sharia intervention; it is prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what is the original ruling (asl) of divorce in the Hanafi school?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Recommended (mustahabb)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Obligatory (wajib)

Key Takeaway
Divorce is originally prohibited but Allah made it permissible; this origin makes it the most hated permissible act.

Recommended and Obligatory Divorce
Discusses when divorce becomes recommended or obligatory based on the wife's conduct or husband's incapacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the circumstances under which divorce becomes recommended (mustahabb) or obligatory (wajib) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Divorce can become recommended for a harmful wife and obligatory when good retention is impossible.

While divorce is generally permissible, the Hanafi school assigns different rulings depending on the situation. This lesson examines two specific cases: when the wife is abusive or neglects prayer, making divorce recommended, and when the husband is impotent or cannot fulfill marital duties, making divorce obligatory. Understanding these gradations helps apply fiqh to real marital problems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended case
Read the passage from Ghayat al-Bayan: divorce is recommended if the wife is abusive (saliqa) or abandons prayer and does not uphold limits.
Note that this implies living with such a woman is permissible but divorce is better.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The recommendation is because the wife's behavior harms the husband and the marital relationship. Divorce provides relief.
This is a form of lifting harm.
3
Identify the obligatory case
Read about the eunuch (majbub) or impotent ('aneen): after the wife's request, if good retention is not possible, the judge may compel divorce.
Divorce becomes wajib upon the husband or is executed by the judge.
4
Note the legal mechanism
The passage says: 'if he misses good retention, the judge takes his place, so he must release her with kindness.' This shows the state intervention.
Obligatory here means the husband must divorce or the judge does it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق الأصل فيه الحظر وترك ذلك بالشرع فصار الحل هو المشروع فهو نظير قول صاحب كشف الأسرار : إن الأصل في النكاح الحظر وإنما أبيح للحاجة إلى التوالد والتناسل، فهل يفهم منه أنه محظور فالحق إباحته لغير حاجة طلباً للخلاص منها لقوله تعالى ولا جناح عليكم إن طلقتم النساء ما لم تمسوهن ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٦] وحمله على الحاجة ليس بصحيح. وفي غاية البيان: يستحب طلاقها إذا كانت سليطة مؤذية أو تاركة للصلاة لا تقيم حدود الله تعالى اهـ. وهو يفيد جواز معاشرة من لا تصلي ولا إثم عليه بل عليها ولذا قالوا في الفتاوى : له أن يضربها على ترك الصلاة ولم يقولوا عليه مع أن في ضربها على تركها روايتين ذكرهما قاضيخان، فقد علمت أنه مباح ومستحب وسيأتي أنه حرام بدعي. ويكون واجباً إذا فات الإمساك بالمعروف كما في امرأة المجبوب والعنين بعد الطلب ولذا قالوا : إذا فاته الإمساك بالمعروف ناب القاضي منابه فوجب التسريح بالإحسان وأما شرطه في الزوج فالعقل والبلوغ، وفي الزوجة أن تكون منكوحته أو في عدته التي تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق وهي المعتدة بعدة الطلاق لا المعتدة بعدة الوطء والخلوة وحاصل ما في فتح القدير أن المعتدة التي هي محل للطلاق هي كل معتدة عن طلاق أو بعد تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وبعد ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً فقط، فلا يقع الطلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في هاتين، ولا يقع وينسب فاعله إلى الحمق لما فيه من كفران النعمة والإيذاء المنهي عنه فليست جهة الحظر ساقطة بالكلية كما يوهمه كلام البحر، ولذا كان أبغض الحلال بخلاف قولهم الأصل في النكاح الخطر فإن هذا الأصل ساقط فإنه حرام في الأصل لما فيه من الانتفاع بجزء الآدمي المحترم والاطلاع على العورات، وارتفع هذا الأصل لحاجة التوالد والتناسل وبقاء العالم. أما الأصل في الطلاق فإنه باق لم يسقط بالكلية فبين الأصلين بون بعيد لما قلنا من بقاء الحظر إذا كان بلا سبب أصلاً، ولا يمكن أن يحمل طلاق النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه رضي الله عنهم على فعله بلا سبب أصلاً بأن يكون لغواً وعبثاً بل لا بد من سبب معتبر شرعاً من الأعذار المذكورة ونحوها، فهذا تحقيق المقام بما لا مزيد عليه فاغتنمه والله الموفق
Book of Divorce: The original ruling in it is prohibition, and that was abandoned by the Sharia, so permission became the legislated ruling. It is similar to the statement of the author of Kashf al-Asrar: 'The original ruling in marriage is prohibition, and it was only permitted for the need of procreation and reproduction.' So is it understood from this that it is prohibited? The correct view is that it is permitted even without need, seeking relief from it, due to His statement: 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women while you have not touched them' [Al-Baqarah 2:236]. And interpreting it as for need is not correct. In Ghayat al-Bayan: It is recommended to divorce her if she is abusive and harmful or one who abandons prayer and does not uphold the limits of Allah. It indicates the permissibility of living with a woman who does not pray, with no sin on him but on her. Therefore they said in the Fatwas: He has the right to beat her for abandoning prayer, and they did not say it is upon him, although there are two narrations about beating her for abandoning it, mentioned by Qadikhan. So you have learned that it is permissible and recommended, and it will come later that it is forbidden and innovatory. And it becomes obligatory if good retention is missed, as in the case of a woman of a eunuch or impotent man after her request. Therefore they said: If he misses good retention, the judge takes his place, so he must release her with kindness. As for its condition in the husband: sanity and puberty. And in the wife: that she be his wife or in her waiting period that is a valid place for divorce, which is the waiting period after divorce, not the waiting period after intercourse or seclusion. The gist of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that the woman in waiting period who is a place for divorce is every woman in waiting period after divorce, or after the judge's separation due to one spouse's refusal to accept Islam, or after apostasy of one of them absolutely. So divorce does not occur in a waiting period from annulment except in those two cases, and it does not occur and its doer is attributed to foolishness because of the ingratitude of blessings and the prohibited harm. So the aspect of prohibition is not entirely abrogated, as the language of al-Bahr might suggest. Therefore it is the most hateful of permissible things, contrary to their statement that the original in marriage is danger, for this original is abrogated – it is originally prohibited due to deriving benefit from a respected human part and seeing private parts, and this original was lifted for the need of procreation and survival of the world. As for the original in divorce, it remains, not entirely abrogated, so there is a great difference between the two originals due to what we said of the persistence of prohibition when done without any reason. And it is impossible to attribute the divorce of the Prophet and his companions to doing it without any reason, as something futile and vain; rather, there must be a legally valid reason from the mentioned excuses and the like. So this is the verification of the matter without further addition; seize it, and Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe discussing the original ruling (hukm asli) of divorce. The author begins by stating that the default ruling of divorce is prohibition (hazr), but this prohibition was abandoned by the Sharia such that permission became the legislated ruling. He compares it to marriage, where the original ruling is also prohibition but permissibility came for the need of procreation. Then he clarifies that divorce is permitted even without need, based on the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah which indicates no sin in divorce before consummation. He then discusses recommended divorce (mustahabb) from Ghayat al-Bayan: if the wife is abusive or abandons prayer, it is recommended to divorce her. This also implies that living with such a woman is permissible without sin on the husband. He mentions fatwas about beating her for abandoning prayer. Then he discusses obligatory divorce (wajib) when good retention is missed, like in cases of impotence, and the judge may compel divorce. Then he lists conditions for the husband (sanity, puberty) and wife (being in a valid marriage or in a waiting period from divorce). He notes that a waiting period from annulment (faskh) does not allow divorce except in two cases: separation due to refusal of Islam or apostasy. He emphasizes that the prohibition aspect of divorce is not entirely lifted, which is why it is called the most hateful of permissible things. In contrast, the original prohibition in marriage is completely lifted for the need of procreation. The author concludes that divorce must have a valid reason; it cannot be futile, as the Prophet and his companions only divorced for valid reasons. The passage is rich in legal reasoning and defines the boundaries of permissible divorce.

Key Terms
بدعي (bid'i): Innovatory divorce, which is haram, such as divorcing during menstruation or in a pure period after intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, when does divorce become obligatory (wajib)?
A) When the wife is abusive
B) When the wife abandons prayer
C) When the husband is impotent and good retention is not possible
D) When there is any marital conflict

Key Takeaway
Divorce is recommended to escape harm and becomes obligatory when the marriage cannot serve its purpose.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Divorce and the Valid ‘Iddah
Lists conditions for the husband and wife, and specifies which types of ‘iddah permit divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to specify the essential conditions for a valid divorce in the Hanafi school and distinguish which types of ‘iddah (waiting periods) allow divorce.

Core Idea
Divorce requires sanity and puberty in the husband, and the wife must be in a valid marital bond or in a specific type of ‘iddah.

Not every pronouncement of divorce counts. The Hanafi school establishes clear conditions for the husband and the wife. A key nuance is the type of ‘iddah: only 'iddah from a valid divorce allows further talaq; ‘iddah from annulment or intercourse does not. This lesson clarifies these boundaries to prevent invalid divorces.

Guided Path
1
Extract the husband's conditions
From the passage: 'وأما شرطه في الزوج فالعقل والبلوغ' — the husband must be sane (aqil) and pubescent (baligh).
Insane or prepubescent males cannot divorce.
2
Identify the wife's basic condition
She must be his wife (mankuhah) or in a waiting period that allows divorce.
This means a valid marriage or specific ‘iddah.
3
Distinguish types of ‘iddah
The text clarifies: 'التي تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق وهي المعتدة بعدة الطلاق لا المعتدة بعدة الوطء والخلوة' — only 'iddah from divorce allows talaq, not from intercourse or seclusion.
This is a critical distinction.
4
Learn the exceptions
From Fath al-Qadir: exceptions for ‘iddah after judicial separation due to apostasy or refusal of Islam – those also allow divorce.
Only two exceptions to the general rule.
5
Apply the rule
If a woman is in ‘iddah from a faskh (annulment) other than those two, talaq does not occur and the husband is blamed for foolishness.
Consequence: talaq is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عدة (iddah): Waiting period after divorce; only the iddah from a valid marriage or certain separations allows divorce.

Checkpoint
A woman is in iddah after her marriage was annulled due to a defect. Can her husband validly divorce her during this iddah?
A) Yes, because she is still in iddah
B) No, because this iddah does not allow divorce
C) Yes, if the husband is sane
D) No, because divorce is only allowed during marriage

Key Takeaway
Divorce is only valid when the wife is in a proper marital bond or in an iddah from divorce; otherwise it is void and blameworthy.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
The Remaining Prohibition and the Requirement of a Valid Reason
Explains that the original prohibition is not entirely gone, making divorce the most hateful of permissible things, and requires a valid reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the original prohibition of divorce is not entirely abrogated and why a valid reason is necessary before divorcing.

Core Idea
Divorce's original prohibition persists, making it the most hateful permissible act; it cannot be done frivolously without a valid reason.

Even though divorce is legally permissible, the Hanafi school insists that it must not be done without cause. This lesson examines the concluding part of the passage, which emphasizes that the prohibition aspect remains, contrasting with marriage. The Prophet and his companions only divorced for valid reasons, establishing a sunnah of restraint. Understanding this helps prevent misuse of the license.

Guided Path
1
Catch the key phrase
The text says: 'فليست جهة الحظر ساقطة بالكلية' – the aspect of prohibition is not entirely abrogated.
This is the central point of this section.
2
Understand the hadith reference
Divorce is referred to as 'أبغض الحلال' (the most hateful of permissible things). This hadith is cited to show the ethical weight.
It is permissible but severely disliked.
3
Contrast with marriage
Marriage's original prohibition was completely lifted for procreation. Divorce's was not fully lifted because it involves harm (idha') and ingratitude (kufran al-ni'mah).
This is why there remains a residual dislike.
4
Requirement of a valid reason
The Prophet and companions did not divorce without a valid cause (udhr). Divorce without reason would be futile (laghw) and impermissible.
Examples of valid reasons from earlier: abuse, impotence, etc.
5
Apply the principle
Therefore, a Muslim should not divorce without a sound Sharia-recognized reason. Doing so approaches the original prohibition.
This protects the institution of marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق الأصل فيه الحظر وترك ذلك بالشرع فصار الحل هو المشروع فهو نظير قول صاحب كشف الأسرار : إن الأصل في النكاح الحظر وإنما أبيح للحاجة إلى التوالد والتناسل، فهل يفهم منه أنه محظور فالحق إباحته لغير حاجة طلباً للخلاص منها لقوله تعالى ولا جناح عليكم إن طلقتم النساء ما لم تمسوهن ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٦] وحمله على الحاجة ليس بصحيح. وفي غاية البيان: يستحب طلاقها إذا كانت سليطة مؤذية أو تاركة للصلاة لا تقيم حدود الله تعالى اهـ. وهو يفيد جواز معاشرة من لا تصلي ولا إثم عليه بل عليها ولذا قالوا في الفتاوى : له أن يضربها على ترك الصلاة ولم يقولوا عليه مع أن في ضربها على تركها روايتين ذكرهما قاضيخان، فقد علمت أنه مباح ومستحب وسيأتي أنه حرام بدعي. ويكون واجباً إذا فات الإمساك بالمعروف كما في امرأة المجبوب والعنين بعد الطلب ولذا قالوا : إذا فاته الإمساك بالمعروف ناب القاضي منابه فوجب التسريح بالإحسان وأما شرطه في الزوج فالعقل والبلوغ، وفي الزوجة أن تكون منكوحته أو في عدته التي تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق وهي المعتدة بعدة الطلاق لا المعتدة بعدة الوطء والخلوة وحاصل ما في فتح القدير أن المعتدة التي هي محل للطلاق هي كل معتدة عن طلاق أو بعد تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وبعد ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً فقط، فلا يقع الطلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في هاتين، ولا يقع وينسب فاعله إلى الحمق لما فيه من كفران النعمة والإيذاء المنهي عنه فليست جهة الحظر ساقطة بالكلية كما يوهمه كلام البحر، ولذا كان أبغض الحلال بخلاف قولهم الأصل في النكاح الخطر فإن هذا الأصل ساقط فإنه حرام في الأصل لما فيه من الانتفاع بجزء الآدمي المحترم والاطلاع على العورات، وارتفع هذا الأصل لحاجة التوالد والتناسل وبقاء العالم. أما الأصل في الطلاق فإنه باق لم يسقط بالكلية فبين الأصلين بون بعيد لما قلنا من بقاء الحظر إذا كان بلا سبب أصلاً، ولا يمكن أن يحمل طلاق النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه رضي الله عنهم على فعله بلا سبب أصلاً بأن يكون لغواً وعبثاً بل لا بد من سبب معتبر شرعاً من الأعذار المذكورة ونحوها، فهذا تحقيق المقام بما لا مزيد عليه فاغتنمه والله الموفق

And in the wife: that she be his wife or in her waiting period that is a valid place for divorce, which is the waiting period after divorce, not the waiting period after intercourse or seclusion. The gist of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that the woman in waiting period who is a place for divorce is every woman in waiting period after divorce, or after the judge's separation due to one spouse's refusal to accept Islam, or after apostasy of one of them absolutely. So divorce does not occur in a waiting period from annulment except in those two cases, and it does not occur and its doer is attributed to foolishness because of the ingratitude of blessings and the prohibited harm. So the aspect of prohibition is not entirely abrogated, as the language of al-Bahr might suggest. Therefore it is the most hateful of permissible things, contrary to their statement that the original in marriage is danger, for this original is abrogated – it is originally prohibited due to deriving benefit from a respected human part and seeing private parts, and this original was lifted for the need of procreation and survival of the world. As for the original in divorce, it remains, not entirely abrogated, so there is a great difference between the two originals due to what we said of the persistence of prohibition when done without any reason. And it is impossible to attribute the divorce of the Prophet and his companions to doing it without any reason, as something futile and vain; rather, there must be a legally valid reason from the mentioned excuses and the like. So this is the verification of the matter without further addition; seize it, and Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe discussing the original ruling (hukm asli) of divorce. The author begins by stating that the default ruling of divorce is prohibition (hazr), but this prohibition was abandoned by the Sharia such that permission became the legislated ruling. He compares it to marriage, where the original ruling is also prohibition but permissibility came for the need of procreation. Then he clarifies that divorce is permitted even without need, based on the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah which indicates no sin in divorce before consummation. He then discusses recommended divorce (mustahabb) from Ghayat al-Bayan: if the wife is abusive or abandons prayer, it is recommended to divorce her. This also implies that living with such a woman is permissible without sin on the husband. He mentions fatwas about beating her for abandoning prayer. Then he discusses obligatory divorce (wajib) when good retention is missed, like in cases of impotence, and the judge may compel divorce. Then he lists conditions for the husband (sanity, puberty) and wife (being in a valid marriage or in a waiting period from divorce). He notes that a waiting period from annulment (faskh) does not allow divorce except in two cases: separation due to refusal of Islam or apostasy. He emphasizes that the prohibition aspect of divorce is not entirely lifted, which is why it is called the most hateful of permissible things. In contrast, the original prohibition in marriage is completely lifted for the need of procreation. The author concludes that divorce must have a valid reason; it cannot be futile, as the Prophet and his companions only divorced for valid reasons. The passage is rich in legal reasoning and defines the boundaries of permissible divorce.

Key Terms
أبغض الحلال (abghad al-halal): The most hateful of permissible things; a description of divorce due to its proximity to the original prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is divorce called 'the most hateful of permissible things' (أبغض الحلال)?
A) Because it is haram but allowed in necessity
B) Because its original prohibition is not entirely abrogated
C) Because the Prophet disliked it
D) Because it is only allowed for men

Key Takeaway
Divorce is permissible but must be done with a valid reason; the original prohibition lingers, making it the most hated of permissible things.

Conditions for Valid Divorce
Explains conditions for husband and wife, and which 'iddah allows divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid divorce (sanity and puberty for husband, wife being a spouse or in a valid iddah) and identify which types of iddah allow divorce according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Divorce is valid only with a sane, adult husband and a wife in a valid marriage or specific iddah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq sets out the essential conditions for a divorce to take effect. It also clarifies a common point of confusion: not every waiting period (ʿiddah) is a valid place for divorce—only those from a previous divorce or certain separations.

Guided Path
1
Identify husband conditions
The text states that for the husband, two conditions are required: sanity (ʿaql) and puberty (bulūgh). If either is absent, the divorce is invalid.
This excludes minors and the insane.
2
Identify wife conditions
For the wife, she must either be his actual wife (manqūḥah) or in a waiting period (ʿiddah) that is a valid place for divorce.
Not all ʿiddahs qualify.
3
Determine valid ʿiddah types
Only ʿiddah from a divorce (ṭalāq), or from a judge's separation due to one spouse refusing Islam (ibāʾ), or from apostasy (riddah) allow a subsequent divorce. All other annulment (faskh) ʿiddahs do not.
Examples of excluded faskh: option of puberty, lack of compatibility, etc.
4
Recognise the consequence of missing conditions
If any condition is missing, the pronouncement of divorce does not take effect—it is legally void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما شرطه في الزوج فالعقل والبلوغ، وفي الزوجة أن تكون منكوحته أو في عدته التي تصلح معها محلاً للطلاق وهي المعتدة بعدة الطلاق لا المعتدة بعدة الوطء والخلوة وحاصل ما في فتح القدير أن المعتدة التي هي محل للطلاق هي كل معتدة عن طلاق أو بعد تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وبعد ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً فقط، فلا يقع الطلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في هاتين
As for its condition in the husband: sanity and puberty. And in the wife: that she be his wife or in her waiting period that is a valid place for divorce, which is the waiting period after divorce, not the waiting period after intercourse or seclusion. The gist of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that the woman in waiting period who is a place for divorce is every woman in waiting period after divorce, or after the judge's separation due to one spouse's refusal to accept Islam, or after apostasy of one of them absolutely. So divorce does not occur in a waiting period from annulment except in those two cases.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from the commentary sets out the conditions for a valid divorce. For the husband, he must be sane (aqil) and have reached puberty (baligh). For the wife, she must be either his actual wife (manquhah) or in a waiting period (iddah) that is a valid subject for divorce. The valid iddah is only that which follows a revocable divorce (talāq rajʿī), not an iddah following intercourse (wati) or seclusion (khalwah) that did not lead to a valid marriage. The author summarises from Fath al-Qadir that the iddah in which divorce can occur is: (1) iddah after a divorce, (2) iddah after the judge separates a couple due to one spouse refusing Islam (ibāʾ), or (3) iddah after apostasy of either spouse. In all other cases of iddah arising from annulment (faskh) – such as annulment due to option of puberty, lack of compatibility, etc. – divorce does not take effect if pronounced during that iddah. This ruling is based on the principle that an annulment severs the marriage from its beginning, so the iddah is not considered a continuation of the marital bond.

Key Terms
عدة الطلاق (iddah al-talaq): Waiting period after a valid divorce; it is the only iddah in which a subsequent divorce can validly occur.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage; its iddah does not allow further divorce except in two cases (ibāʾ and riddah).
إباء (ibāʾ): Refusal to accept Islam by one spouse; when the judge separates them, the iddah is a valid place for divorce.
ردة (riddah): Apostasy; if one spouse apostatises, the subsequent iddah allows divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of iddah does divorce validly occur according to this passage?
A) In any iddah from any separation
B) Only in iddah from a valid divorce or certain separations (ibāʾ or riddah)
C) In iddah from annulment due to choice of puberty
D) In iddah from a forbidden marriage

Key Takeaway
A valid divorce requires a sane, adult husband and a wife who is either his spouse or in an iddah from divorce, ibāʾ, or riddah.

Categories of Divorce: Hasan, Ahsan, Bid'i
Defines and explains the three types of divorce with reward discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of divorce in Hanafi fiqh and state the ruling (hukm) for each, explaining why reward is associated only with avoiding bid'i.

Core Idea
Sunni divorce is permissible, not worship; reward comes from avoiding the sin of bid'i divorce.

Divorce, though the most hateful of permissible acts, is classified into types based on its timing and conditions. The Hanafi school distinguishes sunni (sunnah) divorce into two grades—ahsan and hasan—and a prohibited innovatory (bid'i) type. This lesson unpacks why divorce is not an act of worship and how a person can be rewarded for restraining himself from sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the passage and list the three types of divorce: ahsan, hasan, and bid'i. Note the defining features of each.
Ahsan: one divorce in a pure period without intercourse, then waiting for 'iddah. Hasan: three divorces in three pure periods. Bid'i: divorce during menstruation or after intercourse in a pure period.
2
Understand the legal status of sunni divorce
The passage clarifies that sunni divorce (hasan and ahsan) is called 'sunni' not because it is recommended worship, but because it is done in a manner that avoids blame. Determine the hukm level: it is mubah (permissible), not sunnah.
This refutes the misconception that sunni divorce earns reward as an act of worship.
3
Analyze the reward mechanism
When a person refrains from bid'i divorce and waits for the sunni time, any reward is for restraining from disobedience, not for the divorce itself. The text gives an analogy: refraining from zina is rewarded for self-restraint, not for the absence of zina.
The key point: reward attaches to avoiding sin, not to performing a mubah act.
4
Apply the definition to evaluate a scenario
Given a hypothetical: A man has a strong desire to divorce his wife during her menstruation (bid'i) but waits until she is pure and divorces her then. Is he rewarded? Explain using the passage.
He is rewarded for restraining himself from sin, not for the divorce itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (تطليقها واحدة في طهر لا وطء فيه وتركها حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن) أي أنه بالنسبة إلى البعض الآخر لا أنه في نفسه حسن فاندفع به ما قيل كيف يكون حسناً مع أبغض الحلال، وهذا أحد قسمي المسنون فإنه حسن وأحسن ومعنى المسنون هنا ما ثبت على وجه لا يستوجب عتاباً لا أنه المستعقب للثواب لأن الطلاق ليس عبادة في نفسه ليثبت له ثواب فالمراد هنا المباح. نعم لو وقعت له داعية أن يطلقها بدعياً فمنع نفسه إلى وقت السني يثاب على كف نفسه عن المعصية لا على نفس الطلاق ككف نفسه عن الزنا مثلاً بعد تهيء أسبابه ووجود الداعية فإنه يثاب لا على عدم الزنا لأن الصحيح أن المكلف به الكف لا العدم كما عرف في الأصول. وفي المعراج : إنما كان هذا القسم أحسن من الثاني لأنه متفق عليه
His statement: '(Divorcing her once in a pure period without intercourse and leaving her until her waiting period expires is ahsan)' i.e., it is relative to another, not that it is good in itself. Thus is repelled the objection: How can it be good while it is the most hateful of permissible things? This is one of the two divisions of sunni (sunnah) divorce, for it is hasan and ahsan. The meaning of sunni here is that which is established in a manner that does not incur reproach, not that it is a means of reward, because divorce is not an act of worship in itself to earn reward; therefore the intended meaning here is permissible. However, if he has a motive to divorce her in a bid'i manner and restrains himself until the proper time, he is rewarded for restraining himself from disobedience, not for the divorce itself, just as restraining himself from adultery after its causes are prepared and motive exists: he is rewarded not for the absence of adultery because the correct view is that he is commanded to restrain, not to not exist, as known in usul. In al-Mi'raj: This division is ahsan than the second because it is agreed upon.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (sharh) explains the classification of divorce into three types: hasan (good), ahsan (better), and bid'i (innovatory). The author comments on a statement from the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) that divorcing once in a pure period without intercourse and then leaving her until her 'iddah expires is 'ahsan' (the better type). He clarifies that it is called 'ahsan' relative to another type, not that it is inherently good, since divorce is the most hateful of permissible things. The term 'sunni' divorce does not mean it is worship earning reward; rather it means it is done in a way that avoids blame. Thus it is essentially permissible (mubah). However, if a person desires to divorce wrongly (bid'i) but refrains until the sunni time, he is rewarded for restraining himself from the sin, not for the divorce act itself. The author analogizes this to refraining from adultery after desire arises. He also mentions that the ahsan type is better than the second type because it is agreed upon (by scholars). This passage clarifies that divorce, while legally permissible, is not a devotional act and reward only comes from avoiding sin.

Key Terms
سني (sunni): Divorce done according to sunnah: not incurring blame, but not an act of worship.
أحسن (ahsan): The better type of sunni divorce: one divorce in a pure period without intercourse.
بدعي (bid'i): Innovatory divorce: prohibited, e.g., during menstruation or in a pure period after intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because he avoids the sin of bid'i divorce by restraining himself
C) Because he performs a recommended act
D) Because he is patient

Key Takeaway
Sunni divorce is permissible, not rewardable; any reward comes from avoiding the sin of bid'i divorce.

Rulings on Divorce During 'Iddah and Types of Talaq
Commentary on conditions for valid talaq during 'iddah and its categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid divorce during 'iddah and explain the ruling on talaq al-dawr (cyclical divorce) with its proof.

Core Idea
Divorce during 'iddah is valid under conditions; cyclical divorce (talaq al-dawr) is valid by consensus.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the complex rulings of divorce (talaq) that occur during the waiting period ('iddah). It clarifies that while some dissolutions during 'iddah do not effect divorce, others do, and the key is to examine the type of prohibition involved. The passage also introduces the concept of talaq al-dawr (cyclical divorce) and affirms its validity based on scholarly consensus (ijma'), citing sources like al-Qunyah. By the end, you will understand the conditions that affect the validity and timing of divorce during 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Divorce pronounced during the 'iddah period. What is the hukm? The separation is deferred until the end of 'iddah for revocable (raj'i) divorce, and immediate for irrevocable (ba'in) divorce.
The act is valid, but its effect is delayed in revocable cases.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? For talaq al-dawr, the proof is ijma' (consensus) as stated in al-Qunyah: 'wa bihi yu'lam anna talaq al-dawr waqi' ijma'an'. The passage also references transmitted reports for the non-occurrence of divorce during 'iddah for certain options.
The consensus established the validity, overriding Ibn Surayj's objection.
3
Analyze the conditions
What are the shurut (conditions) for the wording? According to al-Bada'i', among the conditions of the rukn (the specific wording) is that no exception attaches (istithna) and that divorce has no final limit (ghaya). For example, saying 'from one to three' invalidates the triple pronouncement.
These conditions ensure the pronouncement is definitive and immediate.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there a dispute? Yes, on two fronts: (1) Whether divorce during 'iddah occurs for faskh due to options like puberty—the author sides with non-occurrence. (2) Ibn Surayj of the Shafi'is disputed the validity of talaq al-dawr, but his view is disregarded because of the established consensus.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is resolved by following transmitted reports.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? For cyclical divorce, the Hanafi ruling that it occurs by consensus means that if a husband uses such conditional wording, divorce is effective immediately, whereas a minority view would consider it invalid. For faskh during 'iddah, the difference is whether the woman needs to observe a new 'iddah or not.
The practical effect is in the occurrence and timing of the divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
في
العدة
أحدهما
عن فسخ بحرمة مؤبدة كما إذا اعترضت الحرمة بتقبيل ابن الزوج، وكذا عن فسخ بحرمة غير مؤبدة كالفسخ بخيار العتق والبلوغ وعدم الكفاءة ونقصان المهر وسبي ومهاجرته إلينا. وقد صرح في بحث خيار البلوغ بأن الأوجه وقوع الطلاق في العدة ونبهنا ذلك المحل أن المنقول خلافه فالحق ما ذكره هنا من عدمه. وزاد في البدائع أن من شرائطه شرط الركن وهو اللفظ المخصوص أن لا يلحقه استثناء وأن لا يكون للطلاق انتهاء غاية فإنه لو قال أنت طالق من واحدة إلى ثلاث لم تقع الثلاث عند الإمام. وأما حكمه فوقوع الفرقة مؤجلاً إلى انقضاء العدة في الرجعي وبدونه في البائن. وأما محاسنه فالتخلص به من المكاره الدينية والدنيوية. وبه يعلم أن طلاق الدور واقع كما في القنية من آخر الأيمان. وأما أقسامه فثلاثة : حسن وأحسن وبدعي وأما ألفاظه فثلاثة : وما ألحق به صريح
وكناية وسيأتيان
Book of Divorce. Concerning the 'iddah. One of them [is about] dissolution due to permanent prohibition, like when prohibition intervenes by the son of the husband kissing [the wife], and likewise [about] dissolution due to non-permanent prohibition, like dissolution by the option of emancipation, puberty, lack of suitability, deficiency of dower, captivity, and his emigration to us. And it was explicitly stated in the discussion of the option of puberty that the most apparent is the occurrence of divorce in the 'iddah, and we alerted at that place that the transmitted [view] is contrary to it, so the truth is what he mentioned here: its non-occurrence. And al-Bada'i' added that among its conditions is a condition of the pillar, which is the specific wording, that no exception attaches to it, and that divorce has no final limit; for if he said, 'You are divorced from one to three,' the three do not occur according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. As for its ruling, it is the occurrence of separation deferred until the end of the 'iddah in revocable divorce, and without it in irrevocable divorce. As for its benefits, it is deliverance from religious and worldly disliked matters. And by this it is known that cyclical divorce occurs, as in al-Qunyah from the end of the chapter on oaths. As for its divisions, they are three: good (hasan), best (ahsan), and innovated (bid'i). As for its wordings, they are three: explicit (sarih), and what is annexed to it, and metaphorical (kinayah), and they will come later.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rules of divorce occurring during the 'iddah period. It begins by discussing cases where a divorce is invalidated due to permanent or temporary prohibitions, such as when the husband's son kisses the wife (creating a permanent bar) or due to options like emancipation or lack of suitability. The author notes a dispute: in the option of puberty, some say divorce during 'iddah occurs, but the transmitted position is otherwise, and the correct view here is that it does not. Al-Bada'i' adds a condition that the wording must be free of exceptions and limits; for example, saying 'you are divorced from one to three' does not effect three divorces according to Abu Hanifa. The ruling is that separation is deferred until the end of the 'iddah for revocable divorce, but immediate for irrevocable. A benefit is that it allows escape from religious and worldly troubles, from which we infer that 'cyclical divorce' (talaq al-dawr) is valid, as stated in al-Qunyah. The passage then lists three types of divorce by timing: hasan, ahsan, and bid'i, and three types of wording: sarih, mulhaq (annexed to sarih), and kinayah, which will be explained later. The author follows the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and expands on its rulings.

Key Terms
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death during which a woman cannot remarry.
طلاق الدور (talaq al-dawr): A cyclical divorce where the husband says, 'If I divorce you, then before that you are divorced thrice' – valid by consensus.
حسن (hasan): One of the three types of divorce: three divorces in three separate tuhr periods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is valid by consensus (ijma').
C) It is valid only if the husband intends it.
D) It is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
Talaq al-dawr (cyclical divorce) is valid by consensus, and the condition that the wording have no final limit affects the number of divorces pronounced.

Conditions of Ahsan Divorce (الطلاق الأحسن)
Definition and conditions of ahsan divorce with nuanced exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for ahsan divorce and distinguish it from bid'i and hasan divorce.

Core Idea
Ahsan talaq is a single revocable divorce in a tuhr free of intercourse, with no divorce or intercourse in the preceding menstruation.

The Hanafi school divides sunni divorce into two types: ahsan (best) and hasan (good). This lesson focuses on ahsan, outlining its precise conditions as derived from the sources. Understanding these conditions ensures that one performs divorce in the most praiseworthy manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text defines ahsan divorce as a single revocable divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, followed by waiting for the 'iddah. It is considered sunnah (established practice) and the best form.
2
List the conditions for ahsan
Conditions include: (1) pronouncement during a tuhr (clean period), (2) no intercourse in that tuhr, (3) no intercourse or divorce in the preceding menstruation, (4) the divorce must be revocable, (5) no further divorce until 'iddah expires.
These are derived from al-Bada'i' and other sources.
3
Understand the nuance about third-party intercourse
If someone else (not the husband) has intercourse with the wife by shubha in the tuhr, the divorce becomes bid'i. However, if it is adultery (zina), the divorce remains sunni.
This is based on al-Asbajabi's critique.
4
Recognize what invalidates ahsan status
Divorce during menstruation, in a tuhr where intercourse occurred, or if the previous menstruation had intercourse or divorce, makes the divorce bid'i (innovated) and sinful, though valid.
The text clarifies that even if pregnancy appears, intercourse in that tuhr still makes it bid'i.
5
Compare with other types
Ahsan is the best form. Hasan is three divorces in three tuhrs. Bid'i violates the sunnah and is sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (تطليقها واحدة في طهر لا وطء فيه وتركها حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن) أي أنه بالنسبة إلى البعض الآخر لا أنه في نفسه حسن فاندفع به ما قيل كيف يكون حسناً مع أبغض الحلال، وهذا أحد قسمي المسنون فإنه حسن وأحسن ومعنى المسنون هنا ما ثبت على وجه لا يستوجب عتاباً لا أنه المستعقب للثواب لأن الطلاق ليس عبادة في نفسه ليثبت له ثواب فالمراد هنا المباح. نعم لو وقعت له داعية أن يطلقها بدعياً فمنع نفسه إلى وقت السني يثاب على كف نفسه عن المعصية لا على نفس الطلاق ككف نفسه عن الزنا مثلاً بعد تهيء أسبابه ووجود الداعية فإنه يثاب لا على عدم الزنا لأن الصحيح أن المكلف به الكف لا العدم كما عرف في الأصول. وفي المعراج : إنما كان هذا القسم أحسن من الثاني لأنه متفق عليه
هناك أن هذا في الحربية إذا خرجت مسلمة ثم خرج زوجها بأمان فطلقها لا يقع الخ. راجعه قوله : (وسبي أحدهما. ومهاجرته إلينا إنما لا يقع فيهما لعدم العدة لأن المسبي والمهاجر إن كان الزوج فلا عدة على زوجته الحربية وإن كانت المرأة فكذلك لحلها للسابي باستبراء إن كانت مسبية، وإن كانت مهاجرة فكذلك لا عدة عليها عنده وعندهما وإن كان عليها العدة فهي عدة لا : توجب ملك يد فكانت كالعدة في الفاسد. كذا في الفتح وزاد بعده وكذا لو خرج الزوجان مستأمنين فأسلم أحدهما أو صار ذمياً فهي امرأته حتى تحيض ثلاثاً فتقع الفرقة بلا طلاق فلا يقع عليها طلاقه لأن المصر منهما كأنه في دار الحرب لتمكنه من الرجوع ا. اهـ. وفي كلام المؤلف تسامح إذ قوله «وسبي أحدهما ومهاجرته» يشعر بوجود العدة فيهما وليس كذلك قوله : ( وبه يعلم أن الطلاق الدور واقع) أي بكون التخلص المذكور من محاسنه يعلم وقوعه وإلا لفاتت هذه الحكمة تأمل وصورته أن يقول لها إن طلقتك فأنت طالق قبله ثارثاً وهو واقع إجماعاً كما حرره في منح الغفار عن جواهر الفتاوي، فلو حكم بعدمه حاكم لا ينفذ أصلاً، ولا عبرة بخلاف ابن سريج من أصحاب الشافعي . قلت : وسيأتي ذكر

حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن وثلاثاً في إطهار حسن وسني وثلاثاً في طهر أو بكلمة بدعي بخلاف الثاني فإنه مختلف فيه فإن مالكاً قال بكراهته لاندفاع الحاجة بالواحدة. قيد بالواحدة لأن الزائد عليها بكلمة واحدة بدعي ومتفرقاً ليس بأحسن وسيأتي أن الواحدة البائنة بدعي فالمراد بالواحدة هنا الرجعية وقيد بالطهر لأنه في الحيض بدعي وقيد بعدم الوطء لأنه طهر وطئها فيه بدعي لوقوع الندم باحتمال حملها واستفيد منه أنه لو طلقها في ظهر جامعها فيه بعد ظهور حملها لا يكون بدعياً من هذ القسم لفقد العلة وبه صرح في البدائع، وصرح أنه لو طلقها في طهر لا وطء فيه لكن وطئ في الحيض قبله يكون بدعياً لوجود العلة. وعلم من مقابله أنه لا بد أن يكون الحيض الذي قبل هذا الطهر لا طلاق فيه ولا في بعضه جماع ولا طلاق، فلو قال كما في البدائع الأحسن تطليقها إذا كانت من ذوات الأقراء واحدة رجعية في طهر لا جماع فيه ولا طلاق فيه ولا في حيضه جماع ولا طلاق وتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها لكان أحسن. فإن قلت : عبارة المصنف في طهر لا وطء فيه ولم يقيده بوطئه وعبارة المجمع في طهر لم يجامعها فيه فأي العبارتين أولى؟ قلت : يرد على كل منهما شيء أما على الكنز فالزنا فإنه إذا طلقها في طهر وطئها فيه غيره بزنا فإنه سني مع أنه ما خلا عن الوطء فيه، وأما على المجمع فوطء غيره بشبهة فإن الطلاق في طهر لم يجامعها هو وإنما جامعها غيره بشبهة بدعي كما ذكره الأسبيجابي فكان ينبغي أن يستثني المصنف الزنا ويزيد في المجمع ولا غيره بشبهة، وخرج الحسن بقوله وتركها حتى تمضي عدتها ومعناه الترك من غير طلاق آخر لا الترك مطلقاً لأنه إذا راجعها لا يخرج الطلاق عن كونه أحسن كما ذكره الأسبيجابي . وفي المحيط : لو قال لها أنت طالق للسنة وهي طاهرة من غير جماع ولكن وطئها غيره فإن كان زنا وقع في هذا الطهر وإن كان بشبهة لم يقع .
قوله : ( وثلاثا في إطهار حسن وسني) أي تطليقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار حسن وسني، وقد قدمنا أن كلاً من الحسن والأحسن سني فتخصيص هذا باسم إطلاق السنة لا وجه له والمناسب تمييزه بالمفضول من طلاقي السنة. كذا في فتح القدير لكن مشايخنا إنما خصوه باسم السنة لما أنه ورد في واقعه ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما «ما هكذا أمرك الله قد أخطأت السنة». السنة أن تستقبل الطهر فتطلق لكل قرء .تطليقة وخصوا الأول باسم الأحسن لما روي عن إبراهيم النخعي أن أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا يستحبون أن لا يزيدوا في
.
هذه المسألة مبسوطاً في الفصل الآتي بعد باب الصريح عند قوله وإن نكحها قبل أمس وقع الآن». قوله : (لكن مشايخنا إنما خصوه باسم السنة لما أنه ورد الخ قال في النهر : لو قيل إنه إنما خص الحسن بهذا ليعلم أنه في الأحسن سني بالأولى لكان في الجواب أولى ا.هـ. ومثله في الشرنبلالية بزيادة حيث قال : والجواب أنه لما كان من المعلوم أن الأحسن سني بالإجماع لم يحتج إلى التصريح بكونه سنياً، وصرح يكون الحسن سنياً لدفع قول مالك إنه ليس بسني لا لأنه عندنا سني دون الأول. كذا أفاده شيخنا ا هـ .
His saying: (Divorcing her once in a tuhr without intercourse and leaving her until her 'iddah expires is 'ahsan') – meaning it is 'ahsan relative to another [type], not that it is inherently good; thus what was said is repelled: how can it be good while it is the most detested of permissible things? And this is one of the two divisions of the sunnah [divorce], for it is hasan and ahsan. The meaning of 'sunnah' here is that it is established in a way that does not incur blame, not that it entails reward, because divorce is not an act of worship in itself to have reward; so what is meant here is permissible (mubah). However, if he had the motive to divorce her in a bid'i manner, and he refrained until the sunni time, he is rewarded for restraining himself from sin, not for the divorce itself – like restraining from adultery after its causes and motive are present; he is rewarded not for the absence of adultery because the correct [view] is that the obligated is the restraint, not the absence, as known in usul. And in al-Mi'raj: This division is only ahsan than the second because it is agreed upon. There [it is stated] that this [applies] to a warring woman if she came out as Muslim and then her husband came out under aman and divorced her – it does not occur, etc. Refer to his saying: (And the captivity of one of them, and his emigration to us) – they do not occur due to lack of 'iddah, because if the captive or emigrant is the husband, there is no 'iddah upon his warring wife; and if it is the woman, likewise, because she becomes permissible to the captor by istibra' if she is captive, and if she is an emigrant, likewise there is no 'iddah upon her according to him and them [Abu Hanifa and the two companions]; and if there is 'iddah, it is an 'iddah that does not necessitate ownership of hand, so it is like the 'iddah in a fasid [contract]. Thus in al-Fath, and he added thereafter: Likewise if the two spouses go out as musta'minan and one of them becomes Muslim or becomes a dhimmi, she is his wife until she menstruates three times, then separation occurs without divorce, so his divorce does not fall upon her because the one who remains [in dar al-harb] is as if in dar al-harb due to his ability to return. End. And in the author's speech there is looseness, for his saying 'captivity of one and his emigration' suggests the existence of 'iddah in them, but it is not so. His saying: (And by this it is known that cyclical divorce occurs) – i.e., by the fact that the aforementioned deliverance is among its benefits, its occurrence is known; otherwise this wisdom would be lost. Contemplate. Its form is that he says to her: 'If I divorce you, then before that you are divorced thrice,' and it occurs by consensus, as edited in Minah al-Ghaffar from Jawahir al-Fatawa. So if a judge were to rule against it, it would not be executed at all, and no attention is paid to the disagreement of Ibn Surayj of the Shafi'is. I say: And the mention will come later. [Page 416] Book of Divorce: Concerning 'until her 'iddah expires' is ahsan, and three in three tuhrs is hasan and sunni, and three in one tuhr or with one word is bid'i, contrary to the second, for it is disputed: Malik said it is makruh because need is fulfilled by one. It is restricted to one because more than one with one word is bid'i, and separate [divorces] are not ahsan. And it will come that a single irrevocable divorce is bid'i, so what is meant by 'one' here is revocable. And it is restricted to a tuhr because in menstruation it is bid'i. And restricted to the absence of intercourse because in a tuhr in which he had intercourse it is bid'i due to the occurrence of regret at the possibility of pregnancy. From this it is understood that if he divorced her in a tuhr in which he had intercourse after her pregnancy became apparent, it would not be bid'i of this category due to the absence of the cause; and it was stated explicitly in al-Bada'i'. And it was stated explicitly that if he divorced her in a tuhr without intercourse but he had intercourse in the previous menstruation, it is bid'i due to the presence of the cause. And from its converse it is understood that it is necessary that the menstruation before this tuhr have no divorce, nor intercourse in any part of it, nor divorce. So if he said, as in al-Bada'i': 'The ahsan is to divorce her, if she is of those who menstruate, one revocable divorce in a tuhr with no intercourse, no divorce therein, and no intercourse or divorce in its menstruation, and to leave her until her 'iddah ends' – that would be more ahsan. Then if you say: The wording of the author (Kanz) is 'in a tuhr with no intercourse' and he did not restrict it to his intercourse, and the wording of al-Majma' is 'in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her' – which of the two expressions is better? I say: Each has an issue. As for al-Kanz: [it includes] adultery, for if he divorces her in a tuhr in which someone else had intercourse with her by adultery, it is sunni even though it was not free of intercourse. As for al-Majma': [it includes] intercourse by others under shubha, for the divorce in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her but someone else had intercourse under shubha is bid'i, as mentioned by al-Asbajabi. So the author should have excluded adultery and added in al-Majma' 'and no other [person] under shubha'. And the hasan is extracted by his saying 'and leaves her until her 'iddah expires'; its meaning is leaving her without another divorce, not absolute leaving, because if he takes her back, the divorce does not cease to be ahsan, as mentioned by al-Asbajabi. In al-Muhit: If he says to her 'You are divorced according to the sunnah' while she is pure without intercourse, but someone else had intercourse with her – if it was adultery, it falls in that tuhr; if it was shubha, it does not fall. His saying: (And three in tuhrs is hasan and sunni) – i.e., divorcing her three times in three tuhrs is hasan and sunni. And we have already stated that each of hasan and ahsan is sunni, so specifying this with the name 'sunnah' has no justification; the appropriate thing is to distinguish it as the lesser of the two sunni divorces. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. But our mashayikh only specified it with the name 'sunnah' because it occurred in the case of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): 'This is not how Allah commanded you; you have violated the sunnah.' The sunnah is to await the tuhr and divorce one divorce for each menstruation. And they specified the first with the name 'ahsan' because of what was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: that the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to prefer not to increase. This issue is detailed in the coming chapter after the chapter on explicit [divorce] at his saying: 'If he marries her before yesterday, it occurs now.' His saying: (But our mashayikh only specified it with the name 'sunnah' because...) Al-Nahr said: If it were said that he only specified hasan with this to make it known that in ahsan it is sunni a fortiori, that would be a better answer. End. And similar in al-Shurnubulaliyya with an addition: He said: The answer is that since it is known that ahsan is sunni by consensus, there was no need to state explicitly that it is sunni, and he explicitly stated that hasan is sunni to repel the statement of Malik that it is not sunni – not because it is sunni in our view while the first is not. Thus our teacher informed us. End.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the conditions for the best (ahsan) and good (hasan) types of divorce. It begins by defining the ahsan divorce: one revocable divorce pronounced in a tuhr (period of purity) during which no intercourse has occurred, followed by leaving the wife until her 'iddah expires. The author clarifies that 'ahsan' is relative to the hasan type, not that it is itself intrinsically good. He notes that even though divorce is the most detested of permissible acts, this form is considered sunnah (established practice) because it avoids blame. The reward for restraining from a bid'i divorce is for the self-control, not for the divorce act itself, analogous to refraining from adultery. The text then discusses a related point from al-Mi'raj about warring spouses and the effect of captivity or emigration on 'iddah. It clarifies that talaq al-dawr (cyclical divorce) is valid by consensus, as evidenced by the benefit of deliverance from hardships. Next, the passage delves into the conditions for ahsan talaq: it must be a single revocable divorce, in a tuhr free of intercourse (including intercuorse by the husband or others by shubha, but not adultery), and the preceding menstruation must also be free of divorce and intercourse. It contrasts the wording of Kanz al-Daqaiq and al-Majma', noting deficiencies in each, and suggests a more precise definition. Finally, it defines hasan talaq: three divorces in three separate tuhrs. It addresses the terminological issue of why some scholars call this 'sunnah' while calling the first 'ahsan', explaining that this is to counter Malik's view that hasan is not sunnah, and to emphasize that both are sunnah, with ahsan being superior. The commentary draws on al-Bada'i', al-Mi'raj, al-Muhit, Fath al-Qadir, and other Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
الطهر (al-tuhr): The period of purity between two menstruations during which a woman is free from menses and postnatal bleeding.
الطلاق البدعي (al-talaq al-bid'i): Innovated divorce: pronounced during menstruation or in a tuhr in which intercourse has occurred, or three divorces in one utterance.
السني (al-sunni): Divorce that conforms to the Sunnah: either one revocable in a tuhr without intercourse (ahsan) or three in three tuhrs (hasan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for ahsan talaq?
A) Wife must be pregnant
B) Divorce must be irrevocable
C) No intercourse in the preceding menstruation
D) Divorce pronounced in a period of menstruation

Key Takeaway
Ahsan divorce requires a single revocable divorce in a tuhr free of intercourse, with the preceding menstruation also free of intercourse and divorce.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi-Maliki Dispute on Hasan Divorce (الطلاق الحسن)
Dispute over the ruling of hasan divorce between Hanafis and Malik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on hasan divorce and evaluate the Maliki objection.

Core Idea
Hanafis consider hasan talaq (three divorces in three tuhrs) sunni, while Malik considers it makruh because one suffices.

The second type of sunni divorce is hasan: three divorces pronounced one per tuhr. While it is considered acceptable in the Hanafi school, Imam Malik deemed it disliked. This lesson examines the proof and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Hasan divorce is sunni and permissible. It avoids bid'ah and conforms to the practice of the Companions.
2
Identify the Maliki objection
Malik says it is makruh because the need for divorce is fulfilled by one, so three is excessive and disliked.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The hadith of Ibn Umar and the narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i show that the Companions preferred not to exceed one, but they did not forbid three. The Prophet's teaching was about the optimal method, not a prohibition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The hadith does not prohibit three; it only indicates the best practice. The consensus of the Companions supports permissibility of three in three tuhrs.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Malik avoids hasan talaq and considers it makruh; a Hanafi can perform it without any dislike.

قوله: (تطليقها واحدة في طهر لا وطء فيه وتركها حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن) أي أنه بالنسبة إلى البعض الآخر لا أنه في نفسه حسن فاندفع به ما قيل كيف يكون حسناً مع أبغض الحلال، وهذا أحد قسمي المسنون فإنه حسن وأحسن ومعنى المسنون هنا ما ثبت على وجه لا يستوجب عتاباً لا أنه المستعقب للثواب لأن الطلاق ليس عبادة في نفسه ليثبت له ثواب فالمراد هنا المباح. نعم لو وقعت له داعية أن يطلقها بدعياً فمنع نفسه إلى وقت السني يثاب على كف نفسه عن المعصية لا على نفس الطلاق ككف نفسه عن الزنا مثلاً بعد تهيء أسبابه ووجود الداعية فإنه يثاب لا على عدم الزنا لأن الصحيح أن المكلف به الكف لا العدم كما عرف في الأصول. وفي المعراج : إنما كان هذا القسم أحسن من الثاني لأنه متفق عليه

حتى تمضي عدتها أحسن وثلاثاً في إطهار حسن وسني وثلاثاً في طهر أو بكلمة بدعي بخلاف الثاني فإنه مختلف فيه فإن مالكاً قال بكراهته لاندفاع الحاجة بالواحدة. قيد بالواحدة لأن الزائد عليها بكلمة واحدة بدعي ومتفرقاً ليس بأحسن وسيأتي أن الواحدة البائنة بدعي فالمراد بالواحدة هنا الرجعية وقيد بالطهر لأنه في الحيض بدعي وقيد بعدم الوطء لأنه طهر وطئها فيه بدعي لوقوع الندم باحتمال حملها واستفيد منه أنه لو طلقها في ظهر جامعها فيه بعد ظهور حملها لا يكون بدعياً من هذ القسم لفقد العلة وبه صرح في البدائع، وصرح أنه لو طلقها في طهر لا وطء فيه لكن وطئ في الحيض قبله يكون بدعياً لوجود العلة. وعلم من مقابله أنه لا بد أن يكون الحيض الذي قبل هذا الطهر لا طلاق فيه ولا في بعضه جماع ولا طلاق، فلو قال كما في البدائع الأحسن تطليقها إذا كانت من ذوات الأقراء واحدة رجعية في طهر لا جماع فيه ولا طلاق فيه ولا في حيضه جماع ولا طلاق وتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها لكان أحسن. فإن قلت : عبارة المصنف في طهر لا وطء فيه ولم يقيده بوطئه وعبارة المجمع في طهر لم يجامعها فيه فأي العبارتين أولى؟ قلت : يرد على كل منهما شيء أما على الكنز فالزنا فإنه إذا طلقها في طهر وطئها فيه غيره بزنا فإنه سني مع أنه ما خلا عن الوطء فيه، وأما على المجمع فوطء غيره بشبهة فإن الطلاق في طهر لم يجامعها هو وإنما جامعها غيره بشبهة بدعي كما ذكره الأسبيجابي فكان ينبغي أن يستثني المصنف الزنا ويزيد في المجمع ولا غيره بشبهة، وخرج الحسن بقوله وتركها حتى تمضي عدتها ومعناه الترك من غير طلاق آخر لا الترك مطلقاً لأنه إذا راجعها لا يخرج الطلاق عن كونه أحسن كما ذكره الأسبيجابي . وفي المحيط : لو قال لها أنت طالق للسنة وهي طاهرة من غير جماع ولكن وطئها غيره فإن كان زنا وقع في هذا الطهر وإن كان بشبهة لم يقع .
قوله : ( وثلاثا في إطهار حسن وسني) أي تطليقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار حسن وسني، وقد قدمنا أن كلاً من الحسن والأحسن سني فتخصيص هذا باسم إطلاق السنة لا وجه له والمناسب تمييزه بالمفضول من طلاقي السنة. كذا في فتح القدير لكن مشايخنا إنما خصوه باسم السنة لما أنه ورد في واقعه ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما «ما هكذا أمرك الله قد أخطأت السنة». السنة أن تستقبل الطهر فتطلق لكل قرء .تطليقة وخصوا الأول باسم الأحسن لما روي عن إبراهيم النخعي أن أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كانوا يستحبون أن لا يزيدوا في
.
هذه المسألة مبسوطاً في الفصل الآتي بعد باب الصريح عند قوله وإن نكحها قبل أمس وقع الآن». قوله : (لكن مشايخنا إنما خصوه باسم السنة لما أنه ورد الخ قال في النهر : لو قيل إنه إنما خص الحسن بهذا ليعلم أنه في الأحسن سني بالأولى لكان في الجواب أولى ا.هـ. ومثله في الشرنبلالية بزيادة حيث قال : والجواب أنه لما كان من المعلوم أن الأحسن سني بالإجماع لم يحتج إلى التصريح بكونه سنياً، وصرح يكون الحسن سنياً لدفع قول مالك إنه ليس بسني لا لأنه عندنا سني دون الأول. كذا أفاده شيخنا ا هـ .
His saying: (Divorcing her once in a tuhr without intercourse and leaving her until her 'iddah expires is 'ahsan') – meaning it is 'ahsan relative to another [type], not that it is inherently good; thus what was said is repelled: how can it be good while it is the most detested of permissible things? And this is one of the two divisions of the sunnah [divorce], for it is hasan and ahsan. The meaning of 'sunnah' here is that it is established in a way that does not incur blame, not that it entails reward, because divorce is not an act of worship in itself to have reward; so what is meant here is permissible (mubah). However, if he had the motive to divorce her in a bid'i manner, and he refrained until the sunni time, he is rewarded for restraining himself from sin, not for the divorce itself – like restraining from adultery after its causes and motive are present; he is rewarded not for the absence of adultery because the correct [view] is that the obligated is the restraint, not the absence, as known in usul. And in al-Mi'raj: This division is only ahsan than the second because it is agreed upon. There [it is stated] that this [applies] to a warring woman if she came out as Muslim and then her husband came out under aman and divorced her – it does not occur, etc. Refer to his saying: (And the captivity of one of them, and his emigration to us) – they do not occur due to lack of 'iddah, because if the captive or emigrant is the husband, there is no 'iddah upon his warring wife; and if it is the woman, likewise, because she becomes permissible to the captor by istibra' if she is captive, and if she is an emigrant, likewise there is no 'iddah upon her according to him and them [Abu Hanifa and the two companions]; and if there is 'iddah, it is an 'iddah that does not necessitate ownership of hand, so it is like the 'iddah in a fasid [contract]. Thus in al-Fath, and he added thereafter: Likewise if the two spouses go out as musta'minan and one of them becomes Muslim or becomes a dhimmi, she is his wife until she menstruates three times, then separation occurs without divorce, so his divorce does not fall upon her because the one who remains [in dar al-harb] is as if in dar al-harb due to his ability to return. End. And in the author's speech there is looseness, for his saying 'captivity of one and his emigration' suggests the existence of 'iddah in them, but it is not so. His saying: (And by this it is known that cyclical divorce occurs) – i.e., by the fact that the aforementioned deliverance is among its benefits, its occurrence is known; otherwise this wisdom would be lost. Contemplate. Its form is that he says to her: 'If I divorce you, then before that you are divorced thrice,' and it occurs by consensus, as edited in Minah al-Ghaffar from Jawahir al-Fatawa. So if a judge were to rule against it, it would not be executed at all, and no attention is paid to the disagreement of Ibn Surayj of the Shafi'is. I say: And the mention will come later. [Page 416] Book of Divorce: Concerning 'until her 'iddah expires' is ahsan, and three in three tuhrs is hasan and sunni, and three in one tuhr or with one word is bid'i, contrary to the second, for it is disputed: Malik said it is makruh because need is fulfilled by one. It is restricted to one because more than one with one word is bid'i, and separate [divorces] are not ahsan. And it will come that a single irrevocable divorce is bid'i, so what is meant by 'one' here is revocable. And it is restricted to a tuhr because in menstruation it is bid'i. And restricted to the absence of intercourse because in a tuhr in which he had intercourse it is bid'i due to the occurrence of regret at the possibility of pregnancy. From this it is understood that if he divorced her in a tuhr in which he had intercourse after her pregnancy became apparent, it would not be bid'i of this category due to the absence of the cause; and it was stated explicitly in al-Bada'i'. And it was stated explicitly that if he divorced her in a tuhr without intercourse but he had intercourse in the previous menstruation, it is bid'i due to the presence of the cause. And from its converse it is understood that it is necessary that the menstruation before this tuhr have no divorce, nor intercourse in any part of it, nor divorce. So if he said, as in al-Bada'i': 'The ahsan is to divorce her, if she is of those who menstruate, one revocable divorce in a tuhr with no intercourse, no divorce therein, and no intercourse or divorce in its menstruation, and to leave her until her 'iddah ends' – that would be more ahsan. Then if you say: The wording of the author (Kanz) is 'in a tuhr with no intercourse' and he did not restrict it to his intercourse, and the wording of al-Majma' is 'in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her' – which of the two expressions is better? I say: Each has an issue. As for al-Kanz: [it includes] adultery, for if he divorces her in a tuhr in which someone else had intercourse with her by adultery, it is sunni even though it was not free of intercourse. As for al-Majma': [it includes] intercourse by others under shubha, for the divorce in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her but someone else had intercourse under shubha is bid'i, as mentioned by al-Asbajabi. So the author should have excluded adultery and added in al-Majma' 'and no other [person] under shubha'. And the hasan is extracted by his saying 'and leaves her until her 'iddah expires'; its meaning is leaving her without another divorce, not absolute leaving, because if he takes her back, the divorce does not cease to be ahsan, as mentioned by al-Asbajabi. In al-Muhit: If he says to her 'You are divorced according to the sunnah' while she is pure without intercourse, but someone else had intercourse with her – if it was adultery, it falls in that tuhr; if it was shubha, it does not fall. His saying: (And three in tuhrs is hasan and sunni) – i.e., divorcing her three times in three tuhrs is hasan and sunni. And we have already stated that each of hasan and ahsan is sunni, so specifying this with the name 'sunnah' has no justification; the appropriate thing is to distinguish it as the lesser of the two sunni divorces. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. But our mashayikh only specified it with the name 'sunnah' because it occurred in the case of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): 'This is not how Allah commanded you; you have violated the sunnah.' The sunnah is to await the tuhr and divorce one divorce for each menstruation. And they specified the first with the name 'ahsan' because of what was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: that the companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to prefer not to increase. This issue is detailed in the coming chapter after the chapter on explicit [divorce] at his saying: 'If he marries her before yesterday, it occurs now.' His saying: (But our mashayikh only specified it with the name 'sunnah' because...) Al-Nahr said: If it were said that he only specified hasan with this to make it known that in ahsan it is sunni a fortiori, that would be a better answer. End. And similar in al-Shurnubulaliyya with an addition: He said: The answer is that since it is known that ahsan is sunni by consensus, there was no need to state explicitly that it is sunni, and he explicitly stated that hasan is sunni to repel the statement of Malik that it is not sunni – not because it is sunni in our view while the first is not. Thus our teacher informed us. End.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the conditions for the best (ahsan) and good (hasan) types of divorce. It begins by defining the ahsan divorce: one revocable divorce pronounced in a tuhr (period of purity) during which no intercourse has occurred, followed by leaving the wife until her 'iddah expires. The author clarifies that 'ahsan' is relative to the hasan type, not that it is itself intrinsically good. He notes that even though divorce is the most detested of permissible acts, this form is considered sunnah (established practice) because it avoids blame. The reward for restraining from a bid'i divorce is for the self-control, not for the divorce act itself, analogous to refraining from adultery. The text then discusses a related point from al-Mi'raj about warring spouses and the effect of captivity or emigration on 'iddah. It clarifies that talaq al-dawr (cyclical divorce) is valid by consensus, as evidenced by the benefit of deliverance from hardships. Next, the passage delves into the conditions for ahsan talaq: it must be a single revocable divorce, in a tuhr free of intercourse (including intercuorse by the husband or others by shubha, but not adultery), and the preceding menstruation must also be free of divorce and intercourse. It contrasts the wording of Kanz al-Daqaiq and al-Majma', noting deficiencies in each, and suggests a more precise definition. Finally, it defines hasan talaq: three divorces in three separate tuhrs. It addresses the terminological issue of why some scholars call this 'sunnah' while calling the first 'ahsan', explaining that this is to counter Malik's view that hasan is not sunnah, and to emphasize that both are sunnah, with ahsan being superior. The commentary draws on al-Bada'i', al-Mi'raj, al-Muhit, Fath al-Qadir, and other Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
الطهر (al-tuhr): The period of purity between two menstruations during which a woman is free from menses and postnatal bleeding.
الطلاق البدعي (al-talaq al-bid'i): Innovated divorce: pronounced during menstruation or in a tuhr in which intercourse has occurred, or three divorces in one utterance.
السني (al-sunni): Divorce that conforms to the Sunnah: either one revocable in a tuhr without intercourse (ahsan) or three in three tuhrs (hasan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Malik consider hasan talaq makruh?
A) Because it is a bid'ah
B) Because one divorce suffices
C) Because it is forbidden
D) Because it causes regret

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers hasan talaq sunni, while Malik considers it makruh; the practical difference is in the recommended practice.
