Effect of Adding 'Lil-Sunnah' and Similar Phrases to Divorce Pronouncements
Explanation of rulings on 'lil-sunnah' and similar phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of adding 'lil-sunnah' and similar phrases to divorce declarations and distinguish between phrases that indicate sunnah timing and those that require intention.

Core Idea
'Lil-sunnah' is not a direct divorce term; it only affects timing when attached to explicit divorce wording.

When a husband adds phrases like 'lil-sunnah' to a divorce pronouncement, confusion may arise about whether he intended an immediate or delayed divorce. The Hanafi school clarifies that such phrases are not divorce terms themselves; they only indicate that the divorce should be in accordance with prophetic practice. This lesson unpacks the rulings from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on various formulations and their legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Determine the legal effect of the phrase 'lil-sunnah'
Identify whether 'lil-sunnah' is a direct divorce term. The text states it is not, as evidenced by saying 'anti lil-sunnah' alone—no divorce occurs even with intention.
The particle 'lam' (for) makes the phrase ambiguous.
2
Distinguish between 'lam' and explicit time mention
When 'lil-sunnah' is attached to an explicit divorce statement, the lam can be interpreted as indicating sunnah timing. Explicit mention of 'times of the sunnah' does not allow the intention to aggregate divorces; it is treated as a singular time.
The difference lies in ambiguity: 'lam' is open to interpretation, while explicit time is clear.
3
Categorize phrases according to al-Mi'raj's three types
The passage categorizes phrases into three types: (1) those equivalent to 'lil-sunnah' (e.g., talaq al-sunnah, talaq al-'adl), (2) those requiring intention for sunnah timing (e.g., 'fi kitab Allah'), and (3) those where intention is considered inwardly but not in court (e.g., 'ala qawl al-qudat').
This classification helps determine whether the divorce occurs immediately or at the appropriate sunnah time.
4
Apply the distinction between fahish and afhash bid'i divorce
The text explains that bid'i divorce is of two degrees: fahish (e.g., one divorce during menses) and afhash (three divorces at once). Threefold divorce requires intention to be considered sunnah; less than three does not automatically require intention.
This nuanced rule prevents an unintended triple divorce from occurring.

الطلاق. ولو أراد بقوله طالق واحدة وبقوله للسنة أخرى لم يقع لأن قوله «للسنة» ليست من ألفاظ الطلاق بدليل أنه لو قال لامرأته أنت للسنة لا يقع وإن نوى الطلاق. كذا في البدائع . وقيد باللام لأنه لو صرح بالأوقات فقال أنت طالق ثلاثاً أوقات السنة لا تصح نية الثلاث جملة، والفرق أن اللام تحتمل أن لا تكون للوقت فقد نوى محتمل كلامه، وأما التصريح بالوقت فغير محتمل غيره فانصرف إلى السنة الكاملة وهي السنة وقوعاً وإيقاعاً. كذا في المعراج. وهذا يقتضي أن لا فرق بين جمع الوقت وأفراده لأنه مع التصريح به مفرد لا يحتمل غيره كما في المجمع ومراده اللام وما كان بمعناه. فلو قال أنت طالق في السنة أو على السنة أو مع السنة أو طلاق السنة فهو كاللام، وكذا السنة ليس بقيد بل مثلها ما كان بمعناها كطلاق العدل أو طلاقاً عدلاً وطلاق العدة أو للعدة أو طلاق الدين أو الإسلام أو أحسن الطلاق أو أجمله أو طلاق القرآن أو الكتاب.
وذكر في المعراج أنه على ثلاثة أقسام : الأول جميع ما ذكرناه ومنه طلاق التحري، والثاني أن يقول أنت طالق في كتاب الله أو بكتاب الله أو مع كتاب الله ، فإن نوى به طلاق السنة وقع في أوقاتها، وإن لم ينوها وقع في الحال لأن كتاب الله يدل على وقوع الطلاق للسنة والبدعة فيحتاج إلى النية. والثالث أن يقول أنت طالق على الكتاب أو بالكتاب أو على قول القضاة أو على قول الفقهاء أو طلاق القضاة أو طلاق الفقهاء، فإن نوى السنة يدين ويقع في الحال في القضاء لأن قول القضاء أو الفقهاء يقتضي الأمرين، فإذا خصص يدين ولا يسمع في القضاء ا هـ. . وفي مختصر الجامع الكبير للصدر الشهيد : لو قال أنت طالق تطليقة للسنة يقف على محله بخلاف سنية أو عدلة أو عدلية أو حسنة أو جميلة لأنه وصف للواقع وهناك الإيقاع، ولو قال أحسن الطلاق أو أعد له أو أجمله توقف لحرف المبالغة، ولو قال تطليقة حسنة في دخولك الدار وشديدة في ضربك أو قوية في بطشك أو ظريفة في نقابك أو معتدلة في قيامك تتعلق، ولو لم يذكر التطليقة يتنجز لأنه وصفها وتم وصفه ا اهـ. . وفي المحيط : لو قال أنت طالق تطليقة حقاً طلقت الساعة، ولو قال طلاق الحق كان للسنة، وقيد بالسنة لأنه لو قال أنت طالق للبدعة أو طلاق البدعة ونوى الثلاث وقعت للحال، وكذا الواحدة في الحيض والطهر الذي فيه جماع، وإن لم تكن له نية، فإن كان في طهر فيه جماع أو في حال الحيض أو النفاس وقعت واحدة من ساعته، وإن كانت في طهر لا جماع فيه لا يقع للحال حتى تحيض أو يجامعها في ذلك الطهر . كذا في المعراج . وقد بحث
قوله (ومنه طلاق (التحري الظاهر أن المراد به ما ذكره في المتن وهو أن يتحرى طلاقها في الطهر مرة أو ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار قوله فإن نوى به طلاق السنة وقع في أوقاتها) أي وقع ثلاث متفرقة على أوقات السنة والأطهار أو الأشهر. وقوله وإن لم ينو وقع في الحال الظاهر أن المراد به وقوع الثلاث في الحال كما هو ظاهر التعليل. تأمل قوله ( ولو قال أحسن الطلاق الخ) سيأتي قبيل
بعض الطلبة بدرس الصرغتمشية أنه ينبغي أن تقع الثلاث بلا نية إذا كانت في طهر لم يجامعها فيه من غير توقف على الحيض أو الجماع لأنه بدعي. فأجبته بأن البدعي على قسمين فاحش وأفحش كالأحسن والحق السني، فالثلاث أفحش وما دونها فاحش فلا ينصرف إلى الأفحش إلا بالنية. وفي المحيط : لو أمر رجلاً أن يطلق امرأته للسنة وهي مدخولة بها فقال لها الوكيل أنت طالق للسنة أو قال إذا حضت وطهرت فأنت طالق فحاضت وطهرت لم يقع لأنه فوض إليه الطلاق في وقت السنة فلا يملك إيقاعه قبل وقت السنة كما لو قال له طلق امرأتي غداً فقال لها الوكيل أنت طالق غداً لا يقع إذا جاء غد حتى لو حاضت وطهرت ثم قال الوكيل أنت طالق طلقت ولو قال له طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً للسنة فطلقها ثلاثاً للسنة للحال وقعت واحدة، وينبغي أن يطلقها أخرى في طهر آخر ثم يطلقها أخرى في طهر آخر
شيء
اهـ.
Divorce. If he intends by his saying 'one divorce' and by his saying 'for the sunnah' another, it does not occur, because his saying 'lil-sunnah' is not among the words of divorce, as evidence that if he says to his wife 'you are for the sunnah' it does not occur even if he intended divorce. So in al-Bada'i'. And it is restricted to the lam because if he explicitly states times and says 'you are divorced three times at the times of the sunnah' the intention of three altogether is invalid. The difference is that the lam can possibly not be for time, so he intended a possibility of his speech. As for explicit mention of time, it does not admit anything else, so it turns to the complete year (sunnah) in occurrence and effect. So in al-Mi'raj. This entails that there is no difference between aggregate and individual times, because with explicit mention it is singular not admitting anything else as in al-Majma', and his intent is the lam and what is in its meaning. So if he says 'you are divorced in the year/sunnah' or 'on the year' or 'with the year' or 'divorce of the sunnah' it is like the lam. Likewise the year is not a restriction, but similar to it is what is in its meaning like 'divorce of justice' or 'just divorce' etc. He mentioned in al-Mi'raj that it is of three types... etc.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on rulings related to divorce phrases that include 'lil-sunnah' (for the sunnah) and similar expressions. The author begins by stating the ruling: if a man intends one divorce with his words and another with 'lil-sunnah', it does not take effect because 'lil-sunnah' is not a direct divorce term. Evidence: if one says 'you are for the sunnah' no divorce occurs even with intent. The lam (for) is ambiguous, so if he explicitly mentions times like 'at the times of the sunnah', the intention cannot make it cumulative. The passage then categorizes various phrases into three types, citing al-Mi'raj: first includes all mentioned phrases and talaq al-tahari (divorce by careful timing); second involves phrases like 'in the book of Allah' requiring intention for sunnah timing; third includes 'according to the judges' etc. where intention is considered inwardly but not in court. Then quotes from Mukhtasar al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Muhit about specific formulations like 'a true divorce' vs 'divorce of truth', and the discussion about bid'i (innovative) divorce being of two degrees: fahish and afhash. The threefold divorce is afhash and requires intention, while less than three is fahish. Finally, a case from al-Muhit about a proxy being told to divorce for the sunnah but the wife's menstruation and purity do not effect the divorce until the proper time.

Key Terms
للسنة (lil-sunnah): A phrase attached to divorce meaning 'for the sunnah', i.e., in the proper time and manner according to prophetic practice; does not itself effect divorce.
بدعي (bid'i): Innovative divorce, i.e., divorce pronounced at a time or in a manner contrary to sunnah, such as during menses or in a state of impurity.
طلاق التحري (talaq al-tahari): Divorce by careful timing, where one intends to divorce only in a state of purity (tuhr) without intercourse, to follow sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife 'you are divorced for the sunnah' (anti taliq lil-sunnah), what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) One revocable divorce occurs immediately.
B) No divorce occurs unless he intended divorce with the phrase.
C) Three divorces occur if he intended them.
D) The divorce is suspended until the sunnah time.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'lil-sunnah' does not effect divorce by itself, but when attached to an explicit divorce word, it indicates that the divorce should be in the sunnah manner; its effect on timing depends on the type of divorce (single vs. triple) and the presence of other qualifying phrases.

Conditions for Valid Divorce: The Hanafi Position on Joking, Mistake, and Intention
Clarifying the conditions for valid divorce and the proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of divorce in cases of jest, mistake, and lack of intention, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Divorce counts even if joking or mistaken; only kinaya requires intention.

Divorce is one of the most serious acts in Islamic law, yet its validity does not always require serious intent. The Hanafi school, relying on a well-known hadith, holds that a divorce pronounced by a sane adult husband takes effect even if he was joking, mistaken, or did not intend to divorce. This lesson unpacks the conditions and non-conditions from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential conditions
The passage states that the husband must be sane and adult (baligh). These are the only required conditions for the validity of a divorce pronouncement.
The mahal (place) of divorce is the wife, but that is not a condition on the husband.
2
Recognize the non-conditions
The passage lists several things that are NOT required: seriousness, freedom from a condition of option, health, being Muslim, intentionality. For each, a counterexample is given to show that divorce still counts.
The non-conditions are derived from the hadith and logical extensions.
3
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith 'Three things whose seriousness is serious and whose jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and manumission' is cited. It directly proves that joking does not invalidate divorce.
The hadith is ahad but its implication is clear and decisive for the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the rule to specific scenarios
Using the non-conditions, we can determine the validity of divorce in cases of mistake, conditional divorce, divorce by a sick person, etc.
Intention is only required for kinaya (indirect expressions), not for sarih (explicit) words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويقع طلاق كل زوج عاقل بالغ لصدوره. أهله محله من في وهو بيان للمحل وشرائطه، فأشار إلى محله بذكر الزوج فإنه الزوجة ولو حكماً وهي المعتدة كما سبق، وأشار إلى شرطه بالبلوغ والعقل وهو تكليف الزوج، وقد صرح بمفهومه فيما يأتي، ولم يشترط أن يكون جاداً فيقع طلاق الهازل به واللاعب للحديث المعروف «ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: النكاح والطلاق والعتاق (۱) ولا أن يكون خالياً عن شرط الخيار فيقع طلاق شارط الخيار في باب الطلاق بعوض وبغيره لنفسه ولها إلا في مسألة وهي ما إذا شرط لها في الطلاق بعوض لكونه من جانبها معاوضة مال كما سيأتي في الخلع، ولا أن يكون صحيحاً ولا مسلماً فيقع من المريض والكافر، ولا أن يكون عامداً فيقع طلاق المخطيء وهو الذي أن يتكلم بغير الطلاق فيسبق على لسانه الطلاق وكذا العتاق. وروى الكرخي أن في العتاق روايتين بخلاف الطلاق، وروى بشر أنهما سواء وهو الصحيح. الكل من البدائع . ولا أن يكون ناوياً له لأنه شرط في الكنايات فقط. واعلم أن طلاق الفضولين موقوف على
يريد
His saying: (And the divorce of every sane, adult husband occurs because of its issuance. Its subject and conditions... He indicated its subject by mentioning the husband, for it is the wife, even if legally, i.e., the woman in waiting period as before. And he indicated its conditions with puberty and sanity, which are the husband's responsibility. He explicitly stated its opposite in what follows. And he did not require that he be serious, so the divorce of the joker and the player occurs due to the well-known hadith: 'Three things whose seriousness is serious and whose jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and manumission.' Nor that he be free from a condition of option, so the divorce of one who stipulates an option in divorce with compensation or otherwise for himself or her occurs, except in one case: if he stipulates for her in divorce with compensation because it is from her side a financial exchange as will come in khul'. Nor that he be healthy or Muslim, so it occurs from the sick and the disbeliever. Nor that he be intentional, so the divorce of the mistaken person occurs, i.e., one who speaks not intending divorce but it slips from his tongue, and similarly manumission. Al-Karkhi narrated that regarding manumission there are two narrations contrary to divorce, and Bishr narrated that they are the same, which is correct. All from al-Bada'i'. Nor that he have intention, for it is a condition only in kinayat. And know that the divorce of the fudulis (unauthorized agents) is suspended upon...
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the conditions for the validity of divorce as stated in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator explains that the place (mahal) of divorce is the wife, and the conditions for the one who divorces (the husband) are sanity and adulthood (bulugh). He then lists conditions that are NOT required: seriousness (so joking counts, citing the hadith about three things being serious in jest and in earnest), freedom from a condition of option (so making divorce conditional is valid), health (so a sick person's divorce counts), being Muslim (so a disbeliever's divorce counts), being intentional (so a slip of the tongue counts as divorce, contrary to some views about manumission where there are two narrations, but the correct view is they are the same). Intention is only required for kinaya (indirect expressions). The passage concludes with a reference to the divorce of fuduli (unauthorized agent), which is suspended, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): The dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement, valid from any sane adult male regardless of intent or circumstance.
الهازل (al-hazil): The joker: someone who pronounces divorce as a joke without serious intent; his divorce counts according to the hadith.
الكنايات (al-kinayat): Indirect expressions of divorce (e.g., 'You are free' or 'Go to your family') that require intention to effect divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does the divorce of a person who mistakenly says 'I divorce you' when he meant to say something else count?
A) No, because he did not intend it.
B) Yes, it counts because the words are explicit (sarih).
C) Yes, but only if he is sane and adult.
D) No, because he was not serious.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, divorce is valid from any sane adult husband, even if joking or mistaken, with the hadith as proof; only kinaya requires intention.

Divorce Before Consummation with Virtuous Phrases
Ruling on using descriptive phrases for divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for divorce before consummation when using descriptive phrases like 'ahsan al-talaq', and identify the conditions under which it becomes raj'i.

Core Idea
Descriptive phrases like 'best divorce' before consummation yield one revocable divorce at the sunnah time.

Normally, any divorce before consummation is irrevocable (ba'in) and half the dower is due. However, when the husband uses descriptive phrases like 'the best divorce' (ahsan al-talaq) or similar virtuous expressions, the Hanafi school rules that one revocable divorce occurs, but it takes effect at the proper sunnah time, not immediately. This lesson unpacks this exceptional ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the context
The act is the husband uttering a descriptive phrase like 'ahsan al-talaq' to his wife before consummation. Note that the context is before consummation, which normally makes divorce ba'in.
2
State the general rule for divorce before consummation
Recall that in Hanafi fiqh, divorce before consummation is normally ba'in (irrevocable). This is the baseline rule.
3
Recognize the exception for descriptive phrases
The text introduces an exception: uttering phrases that describe the divorce as 'best', 'most beautiful', etc. changes the ruling from ba'in to raj'i.
The phrase must be descriptive; mere intention is not enough.
4
Determine the effect and timing
One raj'i (revocable) divorce occurs, but it is considered to have taken effect at the sunnah time (i.e., after the wife's menstruation if she is in menses, or at a pure time). This defers the divorce's effective date.
If the husband intended three divorces, then three occur but each at its respective sunnah period.
5
Note the applicability regardless of state
Al-Asbijabi confirms that this ruling holds whether the wife is menstruating or in a state of purity, reinforcing the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الطلاق قبل الدخول أنه لو قال أحسن الطلاق أسنه أجمله أعدله خيره أكمله أفضله أتمه يقع رجعياً وتكون طالقاً للسنة في وقتها، وإن نوى ثلاثاً فهي ثلاث للسنة. كذا في كافي الحاكم. وذكر الأسبيجابي أنها تكون رجعية في ظاهر الرواية، سواء كانت الحالة حالة حيض أو طهر، وذكر ما جزم به الحاكم رواية عن أبي يوس يا يوسف .
قوله (وبالفعل لا قال في النهر يمكن أن يكون بالفعل أن يدفع إليها مؤخر صداقها بعد ما طلقها الفضولي اهـ. قال الرملي ومثل ما في البزازية في فتاوى قاضي ظهير لكن نقل في جامع (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الطلاق باب .۹ الترمذي في كتاب الطلاق باب ٩. ابن ماجه في كتاب المقدمة باب . كتاب الطلاق باب ۱۳.
Section: Divorce before consummation. If he says 'the best divorce', 'its most beautiful', 'its most perfect', etc., it occurs as a revocable (raj'i) divorce, and she becomes divorced for the sunnah at its time, and if he intended three, it is three for the sunnah. So in Kafi al-Hakim. And al-Asbijabi mentioned that it is revocable in the apparent narration, whether the condition is menstruation or purity, and he mentioned what al-Hakim firmly narrated from Abu Yusuf... His saying: (And by action, not by speech) al-Nahr said it can be by action such as paying her deferred dower after the fuduli divorced her. End. Al-Ramli said similar to what is in al-Bazzaziyya in Fatawa Qadi Zahir, but it is transmitted in Jami'... narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Talaq, etc.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This is a fassl on divorce before consummation. The author states the ruling: if a man says phrases like 'best divorce' (ahsan al-talaq) or similar before consummation, one revocable divorce occurs, but it takes effect at the sunnah time (i.e., after menstruation if she is in menses, or at a pure time), not immediately. If he intended three, then three divorces occur but they are spread over three sunnah periods. This is from Kafi al-Hakim. Al-Asbijabi reports that it is revocable in the apparent narration, whether she is menstruating or pure. Then there is a gloss about 'by action' (bi al-fi'l) as opposed to speech, where al-Nahr explains it could be by paying the deferred dower after a fuduli (unauthorized agent) divorced her. Then a hadith reference chain is given.

Key Terms
أحسن الطلاق (ahsan al-talaq): An expression meaning 'the best divorce', considered a description; leads to one revocable divorce at the sunnah time.
رجعي (raj'i): Revocable divorce, where the husband can take the wife back during the waiting period without a new contract.
قبل الدخول (qabl al-dukhul): Before consummation of marriage; generally any divorce before consummation is ba'in (irrevocable) and half the dower is due, but these phrases make it raj'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) An immediate irrevocable divorce occurs.
B) One revocable divorce occurs at the sunnah time.
C) Three divorces occur immediately.
D) No divorce occurs because the phrase is unclear.

Key Takeaway
Descriptive phrases like 'best divorce' before consummation produce one revocable divorce at the sunnah time, not an immediate irrevocable divorce.

Divorce Occurs Even in Jest: The Hanafi Position
Expands conditions for valid divorce, stressing that joking does not invalidate it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that divorce is valid without seriousness or intent for sarih (explicit) words and apply it to cases of joking, mistake, and illness, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Joking does not nullify divorce: explicit words of talaq are effective regardless of intent.

Many assume that a divorce pronounced in jest or by mistake is invalid. However, the Hanafi school holds that the seriousness of marriage, divorce, and manumission applies even when taken lightly. In this lesson, we examine the conditions for a valid divorce and the decisive proof from the Prophet's hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorce (talaq). The ruling in the Hanafi school is that it is valid (sahih) and legally effective, provided the husband is sane and adult.
The divorce occurs upon pronouncement of explicit words, regardless of the husband's emotional state.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the well-known hadith: 'Three things their seriousness is serious and their jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and freeing slaves.' This is a hadith recorded by Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah.
Though a hadith ahad, it is considered qat'i in its meaning (dalalah) for the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly equates jest with seriousness for these three actions. Thus, the condition of 'seriousness' (jadd) is not required for divorce; even hazl (jest) triggers the same legal effect.
This reasoning overrides any objections that intent is necessary.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute about whether mistaken pronouncements of 'itaq (freeing slaves) are treated exactly like mistaken talaq. Al-Karkhi reported two narrations on 'itaq, while Bishr held both are the same. The author declares Bishr's view as sahih.
The 'mistaken' (mukhti') case is when one intends to say something else but the word talaq slips out.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Apply the principle: divorce is valid even from a sick person, a disbeliever, a joker, or one who makes a mistake. The only exception where intent matters is for kinayah (ambiguous words), not sarih.
This shows the Hanafi emphasis on the literal utterance over inner state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويقع طلاق كل زوج عاقل بالغ لصدوره. أهله محله من في وهو بيان للمحل وشرائطه، فأشار إلى محله بذكر الزوج فإنه الزوجة ولو حكماً وهي المعتدة كما سبق، وأشار إلى شرطه بالبلوغ والعقل وهو تكليف الزوج، وقد صرح بمفهومه فيما يأتي، ولم يشترط أن يكون جاداً فيقع طلاق الهازل به واللاعب للحديث المعروف «ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد: النكاح والطلاق والعتاق» ولا أن يكون خالياً عن شرط الخيار فيقع طلاق شارط الخيار في باب الطلاق بعوض وبغيره لنفسه ولها إلا في مسألة وهي ما إذا شرط لها في الطلاق بعوض لكونه من جانبها معاوضة مال كما سيأتي في الخلع، ولا أن يكون صحيحاً ولا مسلماً فيقع من المريض والكافر، ولا أن يكون عامداً فيقع طلاق المخطيء وهو الذي أن يتكلم بغير الطلاق فيسبق على لسانه الطلاق وكذا العتاق. وروى الكرخي أن في العتاق روايتين بخلاف الطلاق، وروى بشر أنهما سواء وهو الصحيح. الكل من البدائع . ولا أن يكون ناوياً له لأنه شرط في الكنايات فقط.
He said: (The divorce of every husband who is sane and adult occurs because it issues from its qualified place. He is explaining the place and its conditions. He pointed to the place by mentioning the husband, for it is the wife, even if legally (such as the woman in her waiting period) as previously. He pointed to its condition by puberty and sanity, which is the legal capacity of the husband, and he has explicitly stated its implication later. He did not require that he be serious, so the divorce of the joker and the player occurs due to the well-known hadith: 'Three things their seriousness is serious and their jest is serious: marriage, divorce, and freeing slaves.' Nor that he be free from the condition of option, so the divorce of one who stipulates an option in the chapter of divorce with compensation or otherwise occurs for himself and for her, except in one case, which is when he stipulates for her in divorce with compensation because on her side it is a exchange of property as will come in khul'. Nor that he be healthy or Muslim, so it occurs from the sick and the disbeliever. Nor that he be intentional, so the divorce of the mistaken person occurs, and he is the one who intends to speak something other than divorce and the word talaq slips from his tongue, and likewise free. Al-Karkhi narrated that regarding freeing there are two narrations, unlike divorce, and Bishr narrated that they are equal, and that is correct. All from al-Bada'i'. Nor that he intend it, because it is a condition only in kinayah.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the conditions for a valid divorce. It clarifies that the legal place (mahall) for divorce is the wife (also includes a woman in 'iddah). The conditions on the husband are puberty and sanity; provided these are met, the divorce is effective even if he is joking (hazl) or playing (la'ib), based on the famous hadith. It also lists that a condition of option (shart al-khiyar) does not prevent validity, nor does illness, unbelief, or mistake (mukhti'). The only condition where intention is required is for kinayah (ambiguous words). The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute about mistaken divorce and mistaken freeing of slaves: al-Karkhi held that there are two narrations about freeing, not about divorce; Bishr held both are the same, which is the correct (sahih) position according to the author.

Key Terms
هازل (hāzil): One who is joking or not serious when pronouncing divorce.
مخطئ (mukhtiʾ): One who intends to say something else but the word talaq slips out.
عتاق (itāq): Freeing of a slave; the same ruling applies as talaq in the context of mistaken utterances.
سريح (sarīḥ): Explicit, unambiguous words of divorce that require no intention for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'ثلاث جدهن جد وهزلهن جد' prove regarding talaq?
A) Talaq requires serious intent.
B) Talaq is valid even if done jokingly.
C) Talaq is invalid without witnesses.
D) Talaq is only valid for adult Muslims.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, explicit words of divorce are effective regardless of the husband's mental state (joking, mistake, illness) as long as he is sane and adult.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
6 min
Phrases of Excellence in Divorce: One Revocable Divorce Unless Triple Intended
Ruling on commendatory divorce phrases and intention for triple

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband uses phrases like 'ahsan al-talaq' and identify the effect of intention on the number of divorces.

Core Idea
Praising divorce does not change its legal effect: one revocable divorce, unless triple is intended.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from Kafi al-Hakim: a husband uses commendatory phrases before divorcing. The Hanafi ruling is clear — it counts as one revocable (raj'i) divorce performed according to the Sunnah. However, the husband's intention can turn it into three. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion about the validity and revocability of such pronouncements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrases
List the phrases mentioned in the text: أحسن الطلاق, أسنه, أجمله, أعدله, etc. These are all synonyms for 'the best divorce'.
2
State the default ruling
When uttered without specific intention, these phrases effect one revocable (raj'i) divorce. This is the ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The divorce is valid even if the wife is menstruating, according to al-Asbijabi.
3
Recognize the effect of intention
If the husband intends three divorces with these words, then three divorces occur, and that is considered a sunni triple divorce.
Intention changes the number, not the validity.
4
Identify the source authority
This ruling is transmitted from Kafi al-Hakim and confirmed by al-Asbijabi as the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الطلاق قبل الدخول أنه لو قال أحسن الطلاق أسنه أجمله أعدله خيره أكمله أفضله أتمه يقع رجعياً وتكون طالقاً للسنة في وقتها، وإن نوى ثلاثاً فهي ثلاث للسنة. كذا في كافي الحاكم. وذكر الأسبيجابي أنها تكون رجعية في ظاهر الرواية، سواء كانت الحالة حالة حيض أو طهر، وذكر ما جزم به الحاكم رواية عن أبي يوسف.
Section: Divorce before consummation: if he says 'the best divorce', 'its most beautiful', 'its most complete', 'its most just', 'its best', 'its most perfect', 'its most complete' – it occurs as a revocable divorce, and she becomes divorced according to the Sunnah at its time, and if he intends three, then it is three according to the Sunnah. Thus in Kafi al-Hakim. Al-Asbijabi mentioned that it is revocable in the apparent narration, whether the state is menstruation or purity, and he mentioned what al-Hakim affirmed as a narration from Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a ruling section (fasl) from Kafi al-Hakim about divorce before consummation. It states that when a husband says phrases like 'ahsan al-talaq' (the best divorce) or similar attributes of excellence, it constitutes one revocable (raj'i) divorce performed according to the Sunnah, meaning it occurs in a clean period. If the husband intended three divorces with these words, then it becomes three, and that too is considered Sunni divorce (i.e., triple talaq in one sitting). Al-Asbijabi added that in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), this divorce is revocable regardless of whether the wife is menstruating or pure.

Key Terms
رجعي (rajʿī): Revocable divorce, where the husband can restore the marriage during the waiting period without a new contract.
السنة (al-sunnah): The proper time for divorce: when the wife is in a state of purity (tuhr) without intercourse in that tuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife before consummation 'أحسن الطلاق' and does not intend a specific number, how many divorces occur?
A) One revocable divorce
B) Three divorces
C) No divorce because it is unclear
D) One irrevocable divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that praising divorce does not negate it; such phrases effect one revocable divorce unless triple is intended.
